\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em This is the carry flag. when adding, if the result is greater than 255 or 99 in BCD Mode, then this bit is enabled. In subtraction this is reversed and set to false if a borrow is required IE the result is less than 0  \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em This determines if Interrupts are currently disabled. This flag is turned on during a reset to prevent an interrupt from occuring during startup/\+Initialization. If this flag is true, then the IRQ pin is ignored.  \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
bool \mbox{\hyperlink{class_hardware_1_1_w65_c02_ad42e58d4067c1f778bfdf87af8f0a87e_ad42e58d4067c1f778bfdf87af8f0a87e}{Decimal\+Flag}}\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily  \mbox{[}get, private set\mbox{]}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Binary Coded Decimal Mode is set/cleared via this flag. when this mode is in effect, a byte represents a number from 0-\/99.  \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
bool \mbox{\hyperlink{class_hardware_1_1_w65_c02_ae8a99644c32735c4c267ec3205cc2143_ae8a99644c32735c4c267ec3205cc2143}{Overflow\+Flag}}\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily  \mbox{[}get, protected set\mbox{]}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em This property is set when an overflow occurs. An overflow happens if the high bit(7) changes during the operation. Remember that values from 128-\/256 are negative values as the high bit is set to 1. Examples\+: 64 + 64 = -\/128 -\/128 + -\/128 = 0  \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
bool \mbox{\hyperlink{class_hardware_1_1_w65_c02_af066a29f612f045f2d6a7f8e74bfc0c0_af066a29f612f045f2d6a7f8e74bfc0c0}{Negative\+Flag}}\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily  \mbox{[}get, private set\mbox{]}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Set to true if the result of an operation is negative in ADC and SBC operations. Remember that 128-\/256 represent negative numbers when doing signed math. In shift operations the sign holds the carry.  \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\index{Hardware.W65C02@{Hardware.W65C02}!GetAddressByAddressingMode@{GetAddressByAddressingMode}}
\index{GetAddressByAddressingMode@{GetAddressByAddressingMode}!Hardware.W65C02@{Hardware.W65C02}}
\doxyparagraph{\texorpdfstring{GetAddressByAddressingMode()}{GetAddressByAddressingMode()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily int Hardware.\+W65\+C02.\+Get\+Address\+By\+Addressing\+Mode (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespace_hardware_a20ed8885928dd1f3f9eac50507a162fc_a20ed8885928dd1f3f9eac50507a162fc}{Addressing\+Mode}}}]{addressing\+Mode }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [protected]}}



Uses the Addressing\+Mode to return the correct address based on the mode. Note\+: This method will not increment the program counter for any mode. Note\+: This method will return an error if called for either the immediate or accumulator modes.  


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em addressing\+Mode} & The addressing Mode to use\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The memory Location
\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily bool Hardware.\+W65\+C02.\+Carry\+Flag\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [get]}, {\ttfamily [protected set]}}



This is the carry flag. when adding, if the result is greater than 255 or 99 in BCD Mode, then this bit is enabled. In subtraction this is reversed and set to false if a borrow is required IE the result is less than 0

{\footnotesize\ttfamily bool Hardware.\+W65\+C02.\+Overflow\+Flag\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [get]}, {\ttfamily [protected set]}}



This property is set when an overflow occurs. An overflow happens if the high bit(7) changes during the operation. Remember that values from 128-\/256 are negative values as the high bit is set to 1. Examples\+: 64 + 64 = -\/128 -\/128 + -\/128 = 0
